  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_da4ba962-0ecc-45f1-a124-9d8dd5d19b97'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer4573098203665505802"><em>The Secret History</em> meets <em>Sharp Objects</em> in this stunning debut about murder and glamour set in the ambiguous and claustrophobic world of an exclusive New England prep school.<br/><br/>Death sets the plot in motion: the murder of Nica Baker, beautiful, wild, enigmatic, and only sixteen. The crime is solved, and quickly—a lonely classmate, unrequited love, a suicide note confession—but</span>
  <span id="freeText4573098203665505802" style="display:none"><em>The Secret History</em> meets <em>Sharp Objects</em> in this stunning debut about murder and glamour set in the ambiguous and claustrophobic world of an exclusive New England prep school.<br /><br />Death sets the plot in motion: the murder of Nica Baker, beautiful, wild, enigmatic, and only sixteen. The crime is solved, and quickly—a lonely classmate, unrequited love, a suicide note confession—but memory and instinct won’t allow Nica’s older sister, Grace, to accept the case as closed.<br /><br />Dropping out of college and living at home, working at the moneyed and progressive private high school in Hartford, Connecticut, from which she recently graduated, Grace becomes increasingly obsessed with identifying and punishing the real killer.<br /><br />Compulsively readable, Lili Anolik’s debut novel combines the verbal dexterity of Marisha Pessl’s <em>Special Topic in Calamity Physics</em> and the haunting atmospherics and hairpin plot twists of Megan Abbott’s <em>Dare Me.</em></span>
  <a data-text-id="4573098203665505802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1347730761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1347730761" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1347730761?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=books-claiming-to-be-like-secret-hi">books-claiming-to-be-like-secret-hi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=icky-sex">icky-sex</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1347730761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6477464194509864803">unlike <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History' title='The Secret History by Donna Tartt' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret History</a>, this book has some problems. <br/><br/>i was prepared for it, since so many of the reviews on here have been thumbs-down; people expecting a donna tartt or a gillian flynn and getting something altogether different. and i can't say i hated it - it's a very fast read, and it was a fine summer diversion, but it takes some frustrating shortcuts down build-the-suspense road.<br/><br/>nica baker is sixteen when she is murdered on the grounds of chandler academy, a prep school in hartford, conn</span>
  <span id="freeText6477464194509864803" style="display:none">unlike <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History" title="The Secret History by Donna Tartt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a>, this book has some problems. <br><br>i was prepared for it, since so many of the reviews on here have been thumbs-down; people expecting a donna tartt or a gillian flynn and getting something altogether different. and i can't say i hated it - it's a very fast read, and it was a fine summer diversion, but it takes some frustrating shortcuts down build-the-suspense road.<br><br>nica baker is sixteen when she is murdered on the grounds of chandler academy, a prep school in hartford, connecticut. shortly thereafter, another student kills himself, leaving an incriminating suicide note and the case is officially closed. nica's older sister grace; the shy and cautious opposite to her wild and popular whirlwind, was about to go off to college, but nica's death has rocked her out of orbit and into grief allayed by the narcotizing arms of prescription medication. while her parents fight, drink, and separate, grace makes a lousy decision to attend nica's ex's fourth of july party dressed as nica, and wakes up the next day hungover, newly deflowered, and pregnant with no memory of the sexual act, but with a memory of seeing nica's ghost. <br><br>she makes herself a deal - she will either find nica's real killer before her first trimester elapses, and abort the baby, or if she fails, she will raise the baby as a sort of apology/tribute to nica's memory. <br><br>so, off she goes, in all her 17-year-old investigative fervor, and she discovers all of nica's secrets along with some of her own. <br><br>the other blurb on this is <i>Megan Abbott meets Twin Peaks</i>.<br><br>i'm not sure where the twin peaks comes into play here. except in the "pretty popular high school girl with sexual secrets gets murdered." which is not a concept owned by david lynch. although i did like where grace points out the cliche of it all, especially her deflating of the "homecoming queen" mythos.<br><br>for the most part, it's a fun and twisty thriller. some of it is predictable, some less so. it's one of those "everyone's got secrets, so everyone's a suspect" stories, and i think anolik did a good job strewing suspicion all over the place. the problem is an overreliance upon surfacing memories. grace spent the period following nica's death abusing prescription medication, so she has very few clear memories of that hazy time and she has filled in the blanks with assumptions that are mostly inaccurate. and every time she uncovers a clue or a secret, she suddenly remembers an incident that supports or enhances this "new" knowledge. you can get away with that technique once in a book. use it more than that and it starts feeling contrived. (see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1064015861?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">blair's review</a> for a better version of what i have just said - of how <i>Grace seems to experience memories like other people experience seizures.</i>)<br><br>so it's things like that, and the fact that this doesn't read at all like the voice of a seventeen-year-old (i had to keep reminding myself of the ages of most of the characters - it definitely read more college than high school), and the implausibilities in clue-gathering (how would grace have ascertained the romantic significance of nica's tattoo on first sight?), and some stereotypes in the ethnic blue-collar characters, that made me less of a fan of the book.<br><br>however, there are some things that i thought were great, particularly the relationship between nica and her mother, a sally mann-ish photographer who has obsessively chronicled nica's adolescence in all its tender fumblings and provocative adult posturings. and even though i'd guessed this particular reveal, the scene in the studio was fabulous. huge. generally, all the scenes centered around the family were great - the pressures, the grief, the awkwardness between grace and her father as even basic communication became impossible - it was all incredibly realistic and sad.<br><br>and then there's the scene in which grace becomes pregnant, which seems to be the one that kills the book for many readers. and i completely understand - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it's a really ballsy choice to make your heroine fall for her maybe-rapist. but this is one of those situations which is at once emotionally-charged and hot buttony, but also very very gray. and i think anolik handled it really well, honestly. grace has been an unreliable narrator throughout the entire book, and on the night in question, she was incredibly wasted, but still ambulatory and maybe didn't seem as messed up as she was. and damon's account of the evening does indicate that grace was responding willingly. considering the two of them were both completely in the throes of grief and the shock of "seeing" nica (who was usually intoxicated herself) was probably confusing to damon, i think we can safely say that his <i>intent</i> was never rape, however confused and amnesia-ridden grace was. i think it was written honestly rather than gratuitously, and i think she did a good job of addressing the manylayered complications. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>but overall, it's a fine debut. it has some bumps, but it has strengths to balance them. i always enjoy boarding school murder mysteries, and this one was far from the worst i have read. i liked it, bumps and all.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6477464194509864803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1642596056" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1642596056" />
    <a title="Jaidee " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17295672-jaidee"><img alt="Jaidee " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558439086p2/17295672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1642596056?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaidee " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaidee " href="/user/show/17295672-jaidee">Jaidee </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those that like dark twisted psychological thrillers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jaidee  by: </span>
      my niece has redeemed herself
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17295672-jaidee?shelf=five-stars-books">five-stars-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1642596056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer869469524943895923">5 "snarky, jagged and twisted psychosexual" stars !!!<br/><br/><b> 2016 Honorable Mention Read with High Distinction </b><br/><br/> This is an ancient Greek tragedy in a contemporary private school New England setting.<br/><br/>This book absolutely blew me away. It is sooo raw, soooo sordid and yet so poignant.<br/><br/>A 17 year old girl is murdered and her older sister seeks out her killer.<br/><br/>Do not let the casual contemporary tone fool you. This book is full of primordial emotion. primitive lusts and humans acting out their id impulses in a </span>
  <span id="freeText869469524943895923" style="display:none">5 "snarky, jagged and twisted psychosexual" stars !!!<br /><br /><b> 2016 Honorable Mention Read with High Distinction </b><br /><br /> This is an ancient Greek tragedy in a contemporary private school New England setting.<br /><br />This book absolutely blew me away. It is sooo raw, soooo sordid and yet so poignant.<br /><br />A 17 year old girl is murdered and her older sister seeks out her killer.<br /><br />Do not let the casual contemporary tone fool you. This book is full of primordial emotion. primitive lusts and humans acting out their id impulses in a myriad of ways.<br /><br />The book is full of insight on human behavior and the ugliness that lurks beneath our skin.<br /><br />There are elements of taboo, our link to the spiritual, our desire to connect, our rage let out on others. Ways of hurting our loved ones that are unspeakable, unforgivable and yet happen casually, thoughtlessly and often with little regret. Our need for dominance, to ravage, to eat the other- swallow them whole.<br /><br />Page after page of darkness in order not to get to the light but rather to at least a few minutes of dawn before the clouds roll over and another storm approaches.<br /><br />Fucking brilliant. Read it with an open mind and prepare to be amazed unless you become terrified and denigrate it as just "copycat dark chick-lit".<br /><br />It is so much more!!!! I dare you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="869469524943895923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1055786471" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1055786471" />
    <a title="Diane S ☔" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s"><img alt="Diane S ☔" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598402138p2/4159922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1055786471?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane S ☔" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane S ☔" href="/user/show/4159922-diane-s">Diane S ☔</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1055786471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10502066840267047744">If this book did nothing else it made me so incredibly grateful for the mother I have. Not that my family was perfect by any means but the mother in this book is a piece of work. Seriously she makes Joan Crawford look like a nominee for mother of the year. <br/><br/>grace is the eldest, the quiet sister, the good one. Nica, one year younger is popular, considered by many to be wild. Despite these differences the sisters were close, so when Nica doesn't return home one night and is found dead the next morn</span>
  <span id="freeText10502066840267047744" style="display:none">If this book did nothing else it made me so incredibly grateful for the mother I have. Not that my family was perfect by any means but the mother in this book is a piece of work. Seriously she makes Joan Crawford look like a nominee for mother of the year. <br /><br />grace is the eldest, the quiet sister, the good one. Nica, one year younger is popular, considered by many to be wild. Despite these differences the sisters were close, so when Nica doesn't return home one night and is found dead the next morning it sends Grace into a tailspin.<br /><br />This is much more than a murder mystery, it is about detrimental secrets that come back to haunt, about a woman who is selfish beyond measure, young love and a young woman finding answers, finding peace, a resolution and finally coming into her own.<br /><br /><br />A first novel that is very well done. There are many twists and turns, revelations and red herrings, and I just kept turning the pages. Not sure why this book resonated so with me but I really liked and understood the character of Grace, and felt sorry for the young Nica. Interesting and suspenseful, a very good debut mystery.<br /><br />ARC from publisher.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1064015861" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1064015861" />
    <a title="Blair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/272909-blair"><img alt="Blair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493499323p2/272909.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1064015861?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Blair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Blair" href="/user/show/272909-blair">Blair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24464547-dark-rooms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=first-novels">first-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=2015-release">2015-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272909-blair?shelf=secret-history-esque">secret-history-esque</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1064015861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11845900904638347831">If 2015, so far, has been the year I've started being more selective about psychological thrillers (post-<i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23364977.The_Girl_on_the_Train' title='The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins' rel='nofollow noopener'>Girl on the Train</a>
</i> disappointment) and discovered that I seem to like all the films everyone hates and feel ambivalent towards all the films everyone loves, it might also become the year I finally abandon my persisting affection for any story that resembles, or is compared to, my favourite book, <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History' title='The Secret History by Donna Tartt' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret History</a>.</i> The latest disappointment in what's becoming a very long and uneven line of</span>
  <span id="freeText11845900904638347831" style="display:none">If 2015, so far, has been the year I've started being more selective about psychological thrillers (post-<i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23364977.The_Girl_on_the_Train" title="The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Girl on the Train</a>
</i> disappointment) and discovered that I seem to like all the films everyone hates and feel ambivalent towards all the films everyone loves, it might also become the year I finally abandon my persisting affection for any story that resembles, or is compared to, my favourite book, <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History" title="The Secret History by Donna Tartt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a>.</i> The latest disappointment in what's becoming a very long and uneven line of such stories: Lili Anolik's first novel, a 'stunning debut about murder and glamour set in the ambiguous and claustrophobic world of an exclusive New England prep school'.<br /><br />The prologue of <i>Dark Rooms</i> opens with an arresting line: <i>'The first time I saw my sister after she died was at the Fourth of July party.'</i> Neatly, the first chapter then begins <i>'The last time I saw my sister before she died...'</i> The narrator is Grace, and the late sister is Nica, a couple of years younger but significantly more glamorous, self-assured and (outwardly) mature. Nica is a student at Chandler Academy, a prep school where the sisters' parents both work; Grace is a freshman at university. As we know from the first line, Nica ends up dead, and though her murder appears to be an open-and-shut case - another student hangs himself soon afterwards, leaving a confessional suicide note - Grace is haunted, unable to let it go, and becomes determined to reinvestigate the case and find Nica's real killer by herself. She drops out of college and gets a barely-existent job at Chandler, and the plot of the novel is shaped by Grace's resulting attempts to dig up secrets about her sister, her family, and their friends. <br /><br />This is something of a crossover novel, perhaps a 'new adult' one. Grace and Nica are teenagers, though they don't really read like they are. They sound and act like world-weary adults, as teen characters in these books so often, and so jarringly, do. This is particularly the case when Grace begins working at Chandler; I couldn't help but feel that the story would have been more effective if Grace was maybe five years older and her investigation took place a while after Nica's death, necessitating the uncovering of secrets that were truly buried. The narrative is punctuated by episodes of numbness, ghostly sightings of Nica, and Grace's unconvincing period of drug addiction. The most interesting parts are less to do with the investigation than the background of the story, with the sisters' mother - an intense photographer for whom Nica is an increasingly reluctant subject - standing out as a particularly intriguing example. Another issue is that Grace seems to experience memories like other people experience seizures: she's forever remembering scenes from the past that arrive in 'wave after scalding wave', or else they're 'looming above my head like a tidal wave, threatening to crash down on my life'. It's an inelegant way of working flashbacks into the story when they could simply have been split into separate chapters or demarcated paragraphs. <br /><br />Still, I might have regarded <i>Dark Rooms</i> more highly if - and I am coming to regard this as a sad inevitability in certain types of books - it hadn't been marred by an unnecessary rape scene and subsequent related subplot. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[At a party, extremely drunk and high on prescription drugs, Grace falls/jumps out of a window. She is knocked unconscious and badly injured (she's permanently scarred afterwards). Remembering nothing of the night, she later finds out she is pregnant, and it's clear she must have been raped as she believes herself to be a virgin until finding out about the pregnancy. When Damon is revealed as her rapist, he gives a contradictory account of the night in which he claims that she embraced him and reached up to kiss him, then says she was unconscious when they 'had sex'. Despite that, she almost immediately accepts the blame and concludes that she was possessed by her sister's ghost at the time (!) and Nica was essentially the one who not only consented, but actually 'seduced' Damon. She then ends up in what's painted as a loving relationship with him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The messages sent out by the way the whole episode is portrayed - especially if you consider that, as it features a teenage protagonist, this may be categorised as a YA book - are deeply problematic. I cringe a bit at using that word, but if the shoe fits...<br /><br />Unfortunately, this is what I've taken away from it and what I expect I will remember about it long after I have forgotten the rest of the book. But also, crucially, the rape storyline is unnecessary to the plot. If it was edited out, nothing else about the story would need to be changed, and it serves no purpose at all that I can see. <br /><br />Likened in the blurb to <i>Twin Peaks</i> (why is this cropping up as a reference point so frequently lately?) and Gillian Flynn's <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/66559.Sharp_Objects" title="Sharp Objects by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharp Objects</a>
</i> as well as <i>The Secret History</i>, <i>Dark Rooms</i> is really more comparable to: <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12232938.The_Lovely_Bones" title="The Lovely Bones by Alice Sebold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lovely Bones</a>,</i> for its focus on a teenager's death and similarities between the two books' plot points (a mother abandoning her family after the murder of her daughter, the nature of the pivotal sex scene); <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21495448.Wild_Things" title="Wild Things by Brigid Delaney" rel="nofollow noopener">Wild Things</a>,</i> for its portrait of teenagers behaving badly to extremes that almost defy belief; and <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12224817.The_Year_of_the_Gadfly" title="The Year of the Gadfly by Jennifer Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">The Year of the Gadfly</a>,</i> with which it shares a structure built around a teenage girl setting out to single-handedly investigate an unsolved crime (though it lacks the humour of the latter). <br /><br />I originally rated this book three stars, but the more I think about it - and the fact that I have virtually nothing positive to say about it - the more I'm convinced that was way too generous, so I'm downgrading it to two. I wanted to love it, but it certainly doesn't live up to its own write-up, and for more than one reason, I wouldn't recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11845900904638347831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1152750140" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1152750140" />
    <a title="Heather *Undercover Goth Queen*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen"><img alt="Heather *Undercover Goth Queen*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565231860p2/1256869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1152750140?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather *Undercover Goth Queen*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather *Undercover Goth Queen*" href="/user/show/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen">Heather *Undercover Goth Queen*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=stupid-heroine">stupid-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=no">no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=i-hate">i-hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=dumb">dumb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=word-vomit">word-vomit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=fiction-lit">fiction-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=what">what</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=fpp-bad">fpp-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1256869-heather-undercover-goth-queen?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1152750140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13587483899211472729">Well, thank god that's over.<br/><br/>I've read more than my share of one and two star books lately, so I really wanted to like this. Actually, I thought it was going to be amazing. But it was just awful.<br/><br/>Whose bright idea was it to compare this book not only to <i>The Secret History</i> and <i>Sharp Objects</i>, but also <i>Twin Peaks</i>?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394213911ra/8822876.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The main character jumped to basically every single conclusion she made. And she had flashbacks all the time, usually in the middle of talking to someone. The writing style was so annoying. </span>
  <span id="freeText13587483899211472729" style="display:none">Well, thank god that's over.<br><br>I've read more than my share of one and two star books lately, so I really wanted to like this. Actually, I thought it was going to be amazing. But it was just awful.<br><br>Whose bright idea was it to compare this book not only to <i>The Secret History</i> and <i>Sharp Objects</i>, but also <i>Twin Peaks</i>?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394213911ra/8822876.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The main character jumped to basically every single conclusion she made. And she had flashbacks all the time, usually in the middle of talking to someone. The writing style was so annoying. My GOD it was annoying.<br><br>The best part, though? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It's revealed toward the end that the love interest raped her while she was unconscious at a party. He also impregnated her at this time. After she finds out he's the one who did it, she yells at him and makes him leave her house. Great! But then he proposes (they don't get married though), and she loses the baby (drugs) and they end up living together. Happily ever after! Yay! Oh, and the real murderer never goes to jail because no one tells the police who did it. Awesome. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Seriously, save your time/money on this one. It was bad. I can't believe I made it through this entire book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426866426ra/14112424.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1379389921" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1379389921" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30019-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479137463p2/30019.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1379389921?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/30019-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30019-allison?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30019-allison?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30019-allison?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1379389921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7871360236198640632">This novel was marketed as "Megan Abbott meets Twin Peaks." The Megan Abbott part has to do with the troubled teen girls at the center of the book, Grace, and her murdered sister. The <i>Twin Peaks</i> part has to do with Grace having full blown conversations with her dead sister, and showing up to a party dressed like her. I guess it's not VERY Twin Peaks, just trippy and disturbing, but that's where I think the blurb comes from. <br/><br/>ANYWAYS.<br/><br/>I liked this book a lot. It fits into two of my favorite genres,</span>
  <span id="freeText7871360236198640632" style="display:none">This novel was marketed as "Megan Abbott meets Twin Peaks." The Megan Abbott part has to do with the troubled teen girls at the center of the book, Grace, and her murdered sister. The <i>Twin Peaks</i> part has to do with Grace having full blown conversations with her dead sister, and showing up to a party dressed like her. I guess it's not VERY Twin Peaks, just trippy and disturbing, but that's where I think the blurb comes from. <br /><br />ANYWAYS.<br /><br />I liked this book a lot. It fits into two of my favorite genres, mystery novels, and books set in fancy schools. A few weeks ago, I read a more gut-wrenching novel that also falls into this category called <i>Luckiest Girl Alive</i>. Comparing the two is how I can see <i>Dark Rooms'</i> flaws, because there aren't many. It's a well constructed noir with all manner of sordid things. Where it falters in comparison to <i>LGA</i> is in its protagonist, Grace Baker. She's not a vivid character, and is more defined by how she's not like her sister than by what she does. The book does acknowledge that, but I still didn't care about her on a visceral level. <i>DR</i> was plenty entertaining, but <i>LGA</i> hits you in the gut. Not that you shouldn't read both novels, but definitely space them out more than I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7871360236198640632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1353386387" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1353386387" />
    <a title="Bill Kupersmith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12460952-bill-kupersmith"><img alt="Bill Kupersmith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428792100p2/12460952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1353386387?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bill Kupersmith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bill Kupersmith" href="/user/show/12460952-bill-kupersmith">Bill Kupersmith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12460952-bill-kupersmith?shelf=five-stars-in-2015">five-stars-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12460952-bill-kupersmith?shelf=the-secret-history">the-secret-history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353386387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer437048097715946371">As the ending of Dark Rooms drew near, I could almost hear the voice of George Benson, but with the lyrics just a wee bit altered:<br/><br/>Let me haunt you one more time<br/>Hold me closer, now you're mine<br/>Lady, haunt me one last time<br/>Lady, haunt me<br/>Ho, haunt me, lady.<br/><br/>Indeed Nica Baker is the most haunting schoolgirl character I’ve encountered since Megan Abbott’s Beth Cassidy, but while it takes us a while to find out that Beth is ill-fated, Nica is dead, suddenly & violently, @ the very beginning of this story</span>
  <span id="freeText437048097715946371" style="display:none">As the ending of Dark Rooms drew near, I could almost hear the voice of George Benson, but with the lyrics just a wee bit altered:<br /><br />Let me haunt you one more time<br />Hold me closer, now you're mine<br />Lady, haunt me one last time<br />Lady, haunt me<br />Ho, haunt me, lady.<br /><br />Indeed Nica Baker is the most haunting schoolgirl character I’ve encountered since Megan Abbott’s Beth Cassidy, but while it takes us a while to find out that Beth is ill-fated, Nica is dead, suddenly &amp; violently, @ the very beginning of this story. Tho’ Dark Rooms isn’t a tragedy like Dare Me, it features enough conflicted &amp; sometimes kinky as all-get-out relationships - mother-daughters, brother-sister, sisters-&amp;-(ex&amp;current) lovers including students of both sexes as well as faculty - to provide the plots for a half-dozen Greek tragedies. Like Le Grand Meaulnes it’s a quest story on the mythic level, as the elder sister Grace investigates Nica’s death to find out what really happened. (The authorities fixed the blame on Manny Flores, a student who hanged himself shortly thereafter &amp; then closed the case.) But somewhat like Lexie in Tana French’s The Likeness, Nica’s ghostly presence animates the story, @ times possessing Grace &amp; making her relive Nica’s experiences, even Nica’s sexual relationships. While in the book Grace’s quest is to find Nica’s killer, what fascinates the reader is discovering who Nica really was. As it turns out, the two quests are really one.<br /><br />Nica &amp; Grace’s parents are faculty members @ Chandler, a prep school in Hartford, Connecticut. That is absolutely a brilliant setting for Lili Anolik’s story &amp; characters. Tho’ Dare Me challenged my opinion that only a boarding school can provide the necessary sense of closeness for a great school story, having the characters together 24/7 sets up the character’s relationships much faster. But faculty children are a special case; while not usually boarders, if like Grace &amp; Nica they’ve grown up with the school, their relationship with the school is longer &amp; more intimate than even the boarders’; they are @ once insiders &amp; outsiders to the school community. <br /><br />Chandler is hard to rate on the schools’ league table. It’s clearly better than Amber Dermont's Bellingham in The Starboard Sea. Like Bellingham it provides a haven for better schools’ ejects (Nica’s boyfriend Jamie had been tossed out of Choate for drugs), but it’s an Episcopal foundation with a real chapel &amp; a social conscience that provides scholarships for Hartford area day students - one of whom supplies Nica (&amp; Grace!) with a new boyfriend after she mysteriously breaks off with Jamie. As @ Bellingham, there’re a lot of drugs - both the students &amp; the faculty are dealing &amp; the outing club is getting high in other ways than just hiking the Berkshires, but fortunately Lili Anolik doesn’t share Amber Dermont's obsession with bullies. As Grace the narrator is a very recent graduate, we really cannot expect much of a take on what kind of formation Chandler provides its alumni - it takes many years to discover what role a school plays in our lives.<br /><br />Grace’s father teaches math, apparently badly. (Do they all?) But her mother is a brilliant photography teacher &amp; artist, with Nica as her favorite subject. Nica’s death renders them dysfunctional both as teachers &amp; parents. Dad’s on unpaid sabbatical &amp; working as a hotel bartender; mom’s got a fellowhip @ an artists’ colony &amp; is pursuing her photographic career. Her photos of Nica sound like a combination of Richard Avedon, Diane Arbus, &amp; Robert Maplethorpe - her showing attracts a horde of demonstrators who want to shut it down; they’re not conservative Christians but radical feminists!<br /><br />For once the blurb writers get it sort of right. Dark Rooms has almost the intensity of Dare Me. Like Addy’s, Grace’s narrative voice sounds adolescent North American but torqued to a poetic timbre. Nica is not quite as OTT as Camille Preaker, but if you were haunted by Camille (&amp; by Beth) you’ll go for her too. What it most lacks that I loved in Secret History (&amp; Friendly Fire) was any sign of intellectual &amp; academic achievement @ Chandler. I scarcely felt that Grace or Nica had ever opened a book. As a work of realistic fiction, Dark Rooms has some real problems. Unless you suffer a very (un)lucky hit to the aorta, about the only way you’re likely to die from a .22 caliber bullet to the gut is from sepsis. I couldn’t believe that a slacker druggie like Jamie could get into Princeton even as a legacy (unless squash is much bigger in the Ivy League than one’d ever expect, he’s headed to Lake Forest for sure). I could just barely believe that Grace might have been accepted by Williams. Most especially, it’s totally unlikely that two sisters only a year apart in age &amp; living in the same house could have kept so many secrets as Grace has to find out about Nica. But as mythic quest, Dark Rooms really worked for me. I’m delighted to add it to my school story shelf &amp; eager to see Lili Anolik’s next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="437048097715946371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11276426747929973553">Haunting, poetic and addictive, despite the teenagers who act like they're 25 rather than 16 (I don't even know if I can say <i>that</i>, considering I'm 25 and I'm nowhere near as deep or "mature" as the sisters in <i>Dark Rooms</i>) and the convenient clue-finding that crops up in almost every one of these types of novels. The privileged prep school murder story has been done to death, but I don't think I'll ever really get tired of it. And this one does bring some fresh aspects to the table - the mother-da</span>
  <span id="freeText11276426747929973553" style="display:none">Haunting, poetic and addictive, despite the teenagers who act like they're 25 rather than 16 (I don't even know if I can say <i>that</i>, considering I'm 25 and I'm nowhere near as deep or "mature" as the sisters in <i>Dark Rooms</i>) and the convenient clue-finding that crops up in almost every one of these types of novels. The privileged prep school murder story has been done to death, but I don't think I'll ever really get tired of it. And this one does bring some fresh aspects to the table - the mother-daughter and father-daughter relationships were quite fascinating, and I liked the resolution to the mystery; surprising but not overdone purely for shock value. Though it's probably not exactly worthy of its Tartt and Flynn comparisons, it's the kind of book that will keep you up late into the night in its thrall. </span>

<div id="review_1105794821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1105794821" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1582662-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307033270p2/1582662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1105794821?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/1582662-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1582662-samantha?shelf=2014-books">2014-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1105794821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18072734212309421383">Lili Anolik's "Dark Rooms" pretty much defied all of my expectations. I had anticipated something along the lines of Donna Tartt's "Secret History" and Tana French's recent novel, "The Secret Place," but was pleasantly surprised by the strong and gritty protagonist, and an unpredictable story. “Dark Rooms” centers around Grace Baker, who attends a Connecticut prep school with her younger sister Nica. When Nica is found murdered, the case is solved quickly, but Grace finds herself unsatisfied by </span>
  <span id="freeText18072734212309421383" style="display:none">Lili Anolik's "Dark Rooms" pretty much defied all of my expectations. I had anticipated something along the lines of Donna Tartt's "Secret History" and Tana French's recent novel, "The Secret Place," but was pleasantly surprised by the strong and gritty protagonist, and an unpredictable story. “Dark Rooms” centers around Grace Baker, who attends a Connecticut prep school with her younger sister Nica. When Nica is found murdered, the case is solved quickly, but Grace finds herself unsatisfied by the findings of the local police and commits her attention to discovering the true killer. <br /><br />"Dark Rooms" packs plenty of twists and turns, and definitely some heavy topics. I had a hard time warming up to a lot of characters, but appreciated that none of them fit the stereotypes that you typically see in stories of prep school. <br /><br />The best way I can describe this book is as a "slow burn." Initially readers may be put off my the languid pacing and some of the less than warm and fuzzy characters, but the way the plot eventually spools out will capture your attention. This is one of those novels that after getting to the end and thinking about, I definitely would want to pick up again. <br /><br />Finally, I'd like to thank the publisher for granting me access to an ARC of this novel.<br /><br />Side note: It took me FOREVER to figure out what the cover art was! For all of those that are having issues viewing a larger image of the cover, it's a lighter. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18072734212309421383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1234420272" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1234420272" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5126937-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482805317p2/5126937.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1234420272?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/5126937-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1234420272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7750900501780915326">Grace Baker has always been the girl who causes no trouble. She is a good student, she is a dutiful daughter, and she is a loyal sister. If here is drama to be found, Grace leaves it to her younger sister Nica.<br/><br/>Until, that is, Nica is murdered.<br/><br/>The police think they identify the culprit, so Grace, her parents, Nica's friends, and the school community where they live should find peace, right? Peace is a difficult commodity, however, when the real killer is still running around.<br/><br/>It isn't that Grace's</span>
  <span id="freeText7750900501780915326" style="display:none">Grace Baker has always been the girl who causes no trouble. She is a good student, she is a dutiful daughter, and she is a loyal sister. If here is drama to be found, Grace leaves it to her younger sister Nica.<br /><br />Until, that is, Nica is murdered.<br /><br />The police think they identify the culprit, so Grace, her parents, Nica's friends, and the school community where they live should find peace, right? Peace is a difficult commodity, however, when the real killer is still running around.<br /><br />It isn't that Grace's life, pre-Nica's death, is all that charmed. Her mother is a virago, clearly preferring the company of Nica to that of Grace. She goes so far as to obsessively photograph Nica, whether clothed or naked. Granted, Nica makes a compelling subject. Sexual and sensual, even at age fifteen, Nica commands attention, especially from her boyfriend Jamie.<br /><br />So devoted is Grace to Nica that she forgoes her own attraction to Jamie. Not that Nica is unaware; in fact, Nica knows all too well that Grace loves Jamie, but Nica cannot be bothered to care. Sure, she carries the weight of her mother's photographic expectations, but there is little excuse for Nica's selfishness. She is almost as deplorable as the girls' mother.<br /><br />The days and months after Nica's death are not pleasant for the Baker family. Grace's mother moves out, leaving Grace with a father who increasingly finds comfort in alcohol. Grace numbly approaches her life, dropping out of college and seeking not quite solace, but perhaps more a sense of familiarity in returning home. She is drawn back to Jamie, as well as other friends of Nica's.<br /><br />When Grace happens across something that seems to indicate that Nica's killer has not, in fact, been found, she decides to take on the case herself. To do this, Grace has to team up with people from Nica's past, and she also has to - of course - confront some of her own issues. Foremost of those is Mommie Dearest.<br /><br />To say that Grace's mother makes Cruella DeVille look like the poster child for PETA is a vast understatement. Claire Baker uses her children, and in a most reprehensible way. She also uses her husband. My mother may not have known how to parent children, but at least she never took nudie pics of my teenaged self and tried to make money off of them. Grace, despite her common sense telling her that this is outrageous, finds herself nonetheless a bit jealous. She is the outsider amongst the women in her family, Claire clearly believing that Nica is the shining star. If nothing else, Nica is the means by which Claire will achieve professional acclaim. And if that doesn't give you pause, just read the book and see what else this woman does.<br /><br />Grace also battles her attraction to Jamie. Now that Nica is gone, you would think that the path would be clear. Grace has always felt that Jamie held more than a glimmer of interest for her, but he loved Nica. Does Grace deserve to be the second choice? As conceived by Lili Anolik, no, she does not. She deserves far better. Grace should be first in someone's heart, not a shadowy second to her more arresting sister.<br /><br />There are seedy secrets galore in this book. Just when you think Chandler School can't get more smarmy, Anolik delivers another example that, yes, it actually can. As far-fetched as some of this gets, though, Anolik always makes sure that you believe in Grace. She may make decisions you question, and she may cling to an idea of her mother that will never be realized, but Grace Baker is someone you care about. Deeply so. If she were any less convincing, this book wouldn't stand a chance. But Lili Anolik delivers a character who is sad but not pitiful, hopeful but not gullible, innocent but not naïve. Despite being the older sister, Grace had to be taught by her sister. She watched Nica experience things that would come to her later. And yet Grace is the one who has to grow up the quickest, under the harshest of circumstances.<br /><br />While Grace's growth is the focus of the book, never far away is the mystery. Who killed Nica? Anolik throws out some red herrings, but the killer's identity is never far from your grasp. Much like Grace, you will be asked to trust those she chooses to trust. You also will be asked to accept what Grace accepts. It is a testament of Anolik's writing that you can do this.<br /><br />The titular "dark rooms" are the many trails that Grace must follow as she both uncovers the truth behind her sister's death and, more importantly, the person she is going to be. The thing about darkness, though, is that light is always possible, always right there. Join Grace as she tries to find light.<br /><br /><br /><br />Published on VoxLibris.net<br />@VoxLibris</span>
  <a data-text-id="7750900501780915326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1083711985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083711985" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083711985?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23394234-dark-rooms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=arcs-edelweiss">arcs-edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083711985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1909375073424077788">My rating: 3.5 of 5 stars<br/><br/><b>
  <i>‘I hauled my body along, through the trees, over the fence, toward what I knew–knew because it was there, all of it, in that piercing mechanical wail, knew because it was prophesied in my dream, as elusive as a scent, a shadow, a ghost, knew because it was written in the very blood flowing through my veins—would be as bad as it gets.’</i>
</b><br/><br/>Grace and Nica both attend Chandler Academy, a private boarding school in Hartford, Connecticut where their parents are also teachers. </span>
  <span id="freeText1909375073424077788" style="display:none">My rating: 3.5 of 5 stars<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘I hauled my body along, through the trees, over the fence, toward what I knew–knew because it was there, all of it, in that piercing mechanical wail, knew because it was prophesied in my dream, as elusive as a scent, a shadow, a ghost, knew because it was written in the very blood flowing through my veins—would be as bad as it gets.’</i>
</b><br /><br />Grace and Nica both attend Chandler Academy, a private boarding school in Hartford, Connecticut where their parents are also teachers. Grace was always the quiet sister the resided within the shadow of her younger and wilder sister Nica until a bullet took her life and left Grace suddenly alone. She is troubled by not only her absence, the realization on how much she relied upon her sister but also a sense of bewilderment about who she is supposed to be without her. Grace develops a pill habit that quickly spirals out of control causing her to drop out of college and remain at home. After Nica’s death is pinned on a student who recently committed suicide, Grace doesn’t believe it to be true. After she finds evidence that he couldn’t possibly have killed her she determines it’s up to her to find out who really did.<br /><br /><i>Dark Rooms</i> is a debut novel and while it had some pacing issues and the occasional hiccup, it was quite the engrossing tale. As far as the previously mentioned hiccups, the investigation itself which spans the majority of the novel felt generally ‘off’. When Grace would discover a clue she would either connect the dots in a way that left me completely confounded or would often jump to the strangest and most outlandish conclusions. View Spoiler » The one saving grace is that the main character recognized exactly what she was doing:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘I’ve been pretending I know, careening from conviction to conviction like a human pinball, setting off every light and spark and bell, absolutely positive about one thing, then absolutely positive about another. But, the truth is, the only thing I’m absolutely positive about is that I don’t know anything at all.’</i>
</b><br /><br />It put a new spin on her outlandish conclusions: she was desperate and grasping at straws to find the answers to her sisters death that was plaguing her with uneasiness. There was also another (spoilery) reason for her desperation to complete the investigation and when you took a step back and really looked at what she was going through it ended up making at least a modicum of sense in the madness. The secrets and reasoning behind Nica’s death were dark enough to live up to the title but the additions regarding Nica being her mothers muse in her photography and the lines that were constantly being crossed with her practically stalking her to take candid photos felt a bit gratuitous in the end. This story was a complete knockout as far as the writing is concerned and is definitely worth a read for that alone.<br /><br /><i>Dark Rooms</i> is a mixture of somber tales in suburbia, a murder/mystery thriller and a coming of age novel. Comparisons to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History" title="The Secret History by Donna Tartt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a>, Gillian Flynn’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/66559.Sharp_Objects" title="Sharp Objects by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharp Objects</a> and even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/29593.Megan_Abbott" title="Megan Abbott" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Abbott</a> are what initially intrigued me about this novel. The similarities to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/66559.Sharp_Objects" title="Sharp Objects by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharp Objects</a> is fairly accurate with the story of the seemingly normal teenage girls and the dark family secrets that inevitably change their very makeup but didn’t completely live up to that comparison. All in all, big name comparisons generally always do the book a disservice and while <i>Dark Rooms</i> isn’t a perfect clone, fans of those novels will definitely find some thrill within these pages as I certainly did.<br /><br /><i>I received this book free from Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review. This does not affect my opinion of the book or the content of my review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1909375073424077788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13682874843335856542">Don't make my mistake and be seduced by the well-written synopsis. It's about the only thing that's well-written about this book. DR is poorly written. Not only does it use up every gender/socioeconomic status/sexual orientation/addiction/grief coping mechanism trope that's out there, the author has no sense of voice. Her characters are supposed to be either high school juniors and seniors or college freshmen. They all sound like they are in their mid-twenties. It's not so much their actions (gi</span>
  <span id="freeText13682874843335856542" style="display:none">Don't make my mistake and be seduced by the well-written synopsis. It's about the only thing that's well-written about this book. DR is poorly written. Not only does it use up every gender/socioeconomic status/sexual orientation/addiction/grief coping mechanism trope that's out there, the author has no sense of voice. Her characters are supposed to be either high school juniors and seniors or college freshmen. They all sound like they are in their mid-twenties. It's not so much their actions (given that this takes place at a wealthy, white, upper class boarding school, there is all kinds of permissiveness involved) but the feeling one gets from reading the narration. There is little trace of youth, even world weary youth, which is a serious flaw. As to the central mystery - if you've read one family issues/sexual proclivities/secrets buried/chick lit novel, you won't be that surprised. If you're looking for something in this vein, but far superior, go with Megan Abbot. I'm begging you.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1702986323649513799">Well, this was awful. Normally I feel guilty for giving a book such a low rating, but this book was not just bad, it was offensive. First of all, <i>Dark Rooms</i> is nothing like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History' title='The Secret History by Donna Tartt' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret History</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5886881.Dark_Places' title='Dark Places by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dark Places</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18045891.Sharp_Objects' title='Sharp Objects by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sharp Objects</a>, <i>Twin Peaks</i>, or any of the other "edgy" mysteries out there.   <span id="freeText1702986323649513799" style="display:none">Well, this was awful. Normally I feel guilty for giving a book such a low rating, but this book was not just bad, it was offensive. I had the same problems as everyone else. First of all, <i>Dark Rooms</i> is nothing like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29044.The_Secret_History" title="The Secret History by Donna Tartt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret History</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5886881.Dark_Places" title="Dark Places by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Places</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18045891.Sharp_Objects" title="Sharp Objects by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharp Objects</a>, <i>Twin Peaks</i>, or any of the other "edgy" mysteries out there. The offensive part is that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[reeling from the shock of her sister's murder, the main character blacks out at a party and later discovers she's pregnant. She does not remember ever having sex in her life, so obviously, someone must have raped her while she was unconscious. She doesn't freak out or even wonder about it too much. In fact, she makes a bargain to herself: if she solves the murder, she'll treat herself to an abortion. But if she doesn't, she'll keep the baby and raise it. (Or maybe it was the other way around. It was so weird that I may have the particulars wrong.)<br /><br />Okay, but I still haven't gotten to the offensive part! So she's been hanging out with this guy who used to be her sister's boyfriend. At some point he reveals . . . that he's her rapist! He actually admits, "I had sex with you while you were unconscious." She is sort of mad, but she sort of understands. He was upset! And then . . . they continue to hang out and eventually become boyfriend-girlfriend. WHAT?!<br /><br />The fact that all this happened at all isn't really the offensive part. I am sure that it happens all the time--that people make excuses for their rapists and continue to stay with them. There is probably a way to make this happen in a book without giving the impression that it's a <i>good thing</i>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I also did not like the writing style or even understand what was going on with the murder mystery half the time. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa Klug" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa Klug" href="/user/show/7349048-melissa-klug">Melissa Klug</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7349048-melissa-klug?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7349048-melissa-klug?shelf=2015-audiobook">2015-audiobook</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1262575923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer951872260795270156">I need to cite this book as an example of something about the book world that I find maddening, and also remind myself that I have to stop buying into the blurb game. I chose this book because it was described as all of the following: "Megan Abbott meets Twin Peaks" (fantastic), "for fans of Marisha Pessl" (great!) and "Secret HIstory meets Sharp Objects" (are you kidding me? AWESOME! Sign me up!) i MUST REMEMBER THAT THIS IS MARKETING. BOOKS DESCRIBED AS X MEETS Y ARE NEVER GOING TO BE EITHER X</span>
  <span id="freeText951872260795270156" style="display:none">I need to cite this book as an example of something about the book world that I find maddening, and also remind myself that I have to stop buying into the blurb game. I chose this book because it was described as all of the following: "Megan Abbott meets Twin Peaks" (fantastic), "for fans of Marisha Pessl" (great!) and "Secret HIstory meets Sharp Objects" (are you kidding me? AWESOME! Sign me up!) i MUST REMEMBER THAT THIS IS MARKETING. BOOKS DESCRIBED AS X MEETS Y ARE NEVER GOING TO BE EITHER X OR Y AND IT'S A WARNING SIGN THAT IT'S GOING TO BE DISAPPOINTING. (Also, book industry people, why does everything have to be something else!? Well, maybe because people like me get sucked in. Oh, the cover LOOKS like a Gillian Flynn novel...it must be JUST LIKE IT. I know how this works and STILL it worked on me on this book.) I have a complete inability to abandon books once I start (again, this entire review could better be titled "Lessons Melissa Should Learn") so I stuck it out until the end, but it wasn't for me. Walking away, lessons learned. ((Note: I wonder if I hadn't had the expectations of "Secret History meets Sharp Objects" if I would have liked it more, or given it more slack????))</span>

<div id="review_1080359104" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1080359104" />
    <a title="Taryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13977687-taryn"><img alt="Taryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591322913p2/13977687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1080359104?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taryn" href="/user/show/13977687-taryn">Taryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1080359104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7100291145281401036">The jacket description makes this book sound like a home run: sixteen-year-old prep school student Nica has been murdered. The case is closed, solved tidily without much fanfare, but Nica's sister Grace thinks the real killer is still out there. She sets out to uncover the truth about her sister's death, but she's going to have to dig through a whole lot of dirt before she reaches it. Let me stress that—a LOT of dirt.<br/><br/>It's that sordid, seamy quality that kept me engaged in Dark Rooms despite some</span>
  <span id="freeText7100291145281401036" style="display:none">The jacket description makes this book sound like a home run: sixteen-year-old prep school student Nica has been murdered. The case is closed, solved tidily without much fanfare, but Nica's sister Grace thinks the real killer is still out there. She sets out to uncover the truth about her sister's death, but she's going to have to dig through a whole lot of dirt before she reaches it. Let me stress that—a LOT of dirt.<br /><br />It's that sordid, seamy quality that kept me engaged in Dark Rooms despite some admittedly clunky writing. For my money, the most effective thrillers allow the reader to peek over the investigator's shoulder as she sifts through clues. You may not always know exactly what she's thinking, but it's more exciting that way. The author trusts you as a reader to put some of the pieces together on your own. Unfortunately, Anolik's narrator Grace spouts a constant stream of questions and revelations, spelling out every last detail for us. Under the weight of her internal monologue, the book struggles to maintain the momentum created by its great premise.<br /><br />Still, I kept reading because I had to know what really happened to Nica. She's a fascinating character, even though we only see her through Grace's memories. The girls' mother, a frustrated artist forced into teaching to make a living, takes photos of Nica constantly—and not in a “Let's document these memories!” way, but in a creepy, predatory, voyeuristic way, which their sad-sack father is apparently helpless to stop. Nica also left behind a string of romantic entanglements, some of which she kept secret from everyone, including Grace. There's a major creep factor running throughout the whole book—there were definitely a few bombshells that made my eyes bug out.<br /><br />If you can forgive the long-winded narration, this shocking, twisted story of family dysfunction and long-kept secrets will keep you turning pages into the wee hours.<br /><br />More book recommendations by me at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readingwithhippos.com">www.readingwithhippos.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7100291145281401036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
